Electrical body warmers may be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-infection">Prevention of Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The second important line of management is prevention of infection. This is achieved through environmental control. The room where burns victims are managed must be kept at a high level of cleanliness. Barrier nursing should be practised and visitors controlled. The linen used must be sterile. Antibacterial topical agents, such as silver sulphurdiazine cream, provide protection from bacterial invasion of burns, while penicillin provides early protection from streptococcal infections.</p>
<p>Several studies indicate that prophylactic antibiotics provide no advantage in burns care. The open method of dressing is preferable, in extensive superficial (first-degree) burns, to the</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>closed method, since this method allows the burnt area to dry quickly. It also has the advantage of removing the problem of the dressing adhering to the burnt area.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="providing-nutrition">Providing Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#providing-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Providing nutrition is another important measure. Wherever possible, the gastrointestinal tract should be the primary route of nutrients. This is because this route enhances nutritional effects of prescribed feedings, while at the same time limiting the translocation of bacteria that is likely to occur with parenteral feedings through a central vein. Enteral feeding techniques (oral and nasal gastric tube feeding) allow for a more variable diet to be administered than parenteral (IV) feeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rehabilitation-and-counselling">Rehabilitation and Counselling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rehabilitation-and-counselling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rehabilitation and counselling should be given in order to restore the burned individual to functional status. This requires dedicated expertise to coax and retrain often reluctant burn victims back to a meaningful life. Physical, occupational and speech therapy may be required. The patient will also need to be weaned from life support machines, for example, ventilators.</p>
<p>Some common complications of burns include deep venous thrombosis. The burn team must be alert to its development. Administering a low dose of heparin and using lower extremity compression garments can prevent this. The development of heterotropic ossification (contractures and peripheral nerve palsies) must be prevented by applying daily passive exercises that put the joints through the full range of movement in as far as the patient's condition allows it.</p>
<p>The family should be fully involved in the patient's care. A positive interaction between the patient, family and burns team helps smooth out the serious and predictable life-threatening crisis in the care of the burned individual. Where the surface area burnt is large and burns are severe, survival rate is low. A strong bond of cooperation between the family and the burns team helps to reduce the impact of the patient's demise.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="poisoning">Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The word poison describes a toxic substance. A poison typically causes injury when ingested, although some poisons may be administered in other ways, for example, skin absorption or animal, insect or reptile bites. Poisons from animals, insects or reptile bite are referred to as venoms, however, as you will find out in subsequent sections, not all poisons are venoms.</p>
<p>Poisons usually consist of a single or several toxic components. The main routes of entry into the body are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Through ingestion</li>
<li>Inhalation of atmospheric particulates, for example, while spraying chemicals</li>
<li>Through skin contact with the toxic chemicals</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="poisons-are-classified-into-groups-depending-on-their-source">Poisons are classified into groups depending on their source.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poisons-are-classified-into-groups-depending-on-their-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Did your list include the following groups?</p>
<ul>
<li>Agricultural poisons</li>
<li>Industrial poisons</li>
<li>Household hazards/poisons</li>
<li>Medicinal poisons</li>
</ul>
<p>These groupings are based on sources of poisoning rather than type of toxic substance. For example, under agricultural poisons you have hallogenated insecticides, cholinesterase inhibitors consisting of two distinct chemical groups of compounds, that is, organophosphorus derivative and carbonates. In both groups the chemical differences are of interest, since antidotes useful in treating the organophosphorus type may not work, or may be contradicted in, the treatment of poisoning of the carbonate type.</p>
<p>For these reasons, industries manufacturing insecticides and other pesticides are required by law to provide written literature with each container of the product detailing the first aid treatment and antidotes of the substance they manufacture.</p>
<p>Your role as a health worker is to educate the community so as to create awareness about the methods they can use to prevent poisoning, especially through safe handling and storage of toxic substances. In your previous experience and practice in environmental health you will have experienced various techniques for the prevention and control of poisoning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-and-evaluation-of-poisoning">Diagnosis and Evaluation of Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-and-evaluation-of-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Your first responsibility is to retard absorption or otherwise limit the effects of poison. This forms the basis of first aid in poisoning. After this, you</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>must diagnose the types of poison through history taking and observations and determine whether further treatment is required. In many cases of poisoning, the agent responsible is known. However, the degree or seriousness of the poisoning may need to be verified since, in many instances, the history is inaccurate.</p>
<p>The exact quantity of poison absorbed by the patient will probably be unknown but the clinician may be able to estimate this by examining the container from which the poison was obtained and questioning relatives or coworkers to determine the amount present in the container previously. The missing balance is then assumed as the amount ingested. This is compared with the known lethal dose as per the manufacturer's literature on the container. Where this is not possible, the best thing to do is</p>
<p>to assume that a lethal dose has entered the body and plan the management based on that assumption.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-and-evaluation-of-poisoning">Diagnosis and Evaluation of Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-and-evaluation-of-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In acute poisoning, where a large lethal dose has been ingested, inhaled or come in contact with skin, speed is essential to save life. Acute poisoning should be suspected if:</p>
<ul>
<li>Patient develops symptoms shortly after exposure to a known poison</li>
<li>Patient's history indicates they have been exposed to substance known to have high fatalities</li>
<li>Patient has been exposed to unknown toxic substance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history-and-physical-findings-of-various-poisons-in-children">History and Physical Findings of Various Poisons in Children<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-and-physical-findings-of-various-poisons-in-children" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>History and physical findings</th><th>Most likely poison</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Drug ingestion</td><td>Aspirin, antihistamines, iron tablets, barbiturates</td></tr><tr><td>Alcohol ingestion</td><td>Alcohols</td></tr><tr><td>Dry cleaning</td><td>Chlorinated compounds, petroleum hydrocarbons</td></tr><tr><td>Insecticide use</td><td>Cholinesterase inhibitor pesticides</td></tr><tr><td>Epilepsy</td><td>Anticonvulsants</td></tr><tr><td>Odour of breath:</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Alcohol</td><td>Phenols, cyanide, chloralydrate alcohols</td></tr><tr><td>Acetone</td><td>Lacquer, alcohol</td></tr><tr><td>Coal gas</td><td>Carbon monoxide</td></tr><tr><td>Acrid</td><td>Paraldehyde</td></tr><tr><td>Colour of skin</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Hyperemia</td><td>Cyanide alcohol</td></tr><tr><td>Cherry red</td><td>Carbon monoxide</td></tr><tr><td>Cyanosis</td><td>Aniline, nitrobenzene, nitrate, marking ink</td></tr><tr><td>Pallor</td><td>Benzene, carbon monoxide</td></tr><tr><td>Jaundice</td><td>Mushrooms, quinacrine, nitro compound, phosphorous, carbon tetrachloride</td></tr><tr><td>Temperature</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Increase</td><td>Dinitrophenol</td></tr><tr><td>Decreased</td><td>Chloral hydrates, morphine, barbiturates</td></tr><tr><td>Pulse</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Rapid</td><td>Barbiturates</td></tr><tr><td>Irregular</td><td>Insecticides</td></tr><tr><td>Slow</td><td>Morphine</td></tr><tr><td>Respiration</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Kussmaul</td><td>Salicylates, acetanilid, cinchophen</td></tr><tr><td>Increased</td><td>Dinitrophenol, carbon monoxide, cyanide</td></tr><tr><td>Wheezing</td><td>Cholinesterase inhibitor pesticides</td></tr><tr><td>Convulsions</td><td>Alcohol, insecticides, strychnine</td></tr><tr><td>Vomiting</td><td>Any poison</td></tr><tr><td>Neck stiffness</td><td>Strychnine, cocaine</td></tr></tbody></table>

<p>You will now look at the system examination findings and the poison likely to be responsible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-findings">General Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>General findings may include the following:</p>
<p><strong>Weight Loss</strong> - Chronic poisoning of lead, arsenic, dinitrophenol, mercury and chlorinated hydrocarbons.</p>
<p><strong>Lethargy, Weakness</strong> - Lead, arsenic mercury, chlorinated organic compounds, thiacide diuretics, organophosphates, nicotine, thallium, nitrites, fluorides, botulism.</p>
<p><strong>Fall in Blood Pressure</strong> - Nitrates, nitroglycerin, chlorpromazine, quinine, volatile oils, disulfiran (antabuse) iron salt, methyl bromide, arsine arsenic, fluorides, phosphine, nickel carbonyl, stabine, food poisoning, boric acid, phosphorous.</p>
<p><strong>Rise in Blood Pressure</strong> - Epinephrine, veratrium, ergot, cortisone, vanadium, lead, nicotine.</p>
<p><strong>Pulse Rate</strong> - Fast pulse may indicate potassium, bromate, iron salts, atropine. Slow pulse or irregular pulse may indicate Veratrum, zygademus, digitalis, mushrooms, oleander, nitrite.</p>
<p><strong>Hypothermia</strong> - Dinitrophenol, atropine, boric acid, salicylates, food poisoning, antihistamines, tranquilizers, camphor.</p>
<p><strong>Breath</strong> - Bitter almonds odour may indicate cyanide. A garlic odour may indicate arsine, arsenic, phosphorus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-skin">The Skin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-skin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The skin should be examined for the following indicators:</p>
<p>distress or shock is usually due to methaemoglobinaemia from aniline, nitrobenzene, phenactin, nitrate, bismuth subnitrate, chlorates.</p>
<p><strong>Dry skin</strong> - which is normally due to atropine poisoning.</p>
<p><strong>Jaundice</strong> - caused by liver injury due to carbon tetrachloride, arsenic or other heavy metals, chromates, mushrooms, phenothiazines, sulfanilamides, chlorpromazine, triumtrotolene, aniline, thiazide diuretics, phosphorus jaundice from haemolysis due to: aniline, nitrobenzene, pamaquine, pentaquine, primaquine, benzene, caster beans, jaquility beans, fava beans, phosphine, arsine nickel carbonyl.</p>
<p><strong>Sweating</strong> - which is a result of organic phosphate, insecticides, muscadine and other mushroom poisonings, nicotine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-central-nervous-system">The Central Nervous System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-central-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The central nervous system may be affected, leading to the following manifestations:</p>
<p><strong>Psychosis</strong> - due to Thiazide diuretics, adrenal glucocorticoids, ganglionic blocking agents.</p>
<p><strong>Delirium or Hallucinations</strong> - as a result of alcohol, antihistamines, atropine, lead, cannabis sativa, cocaine, amphetamine, bromides, quinacrine, ergot, sarotonin, ranwolfia, salicylates, phenylbutazone, methyl bromide, DDT, chlordane, barbiturates, boric acid aminopylline.</p>
<p><strong>Depression, Drowsiness or Coma</strong> - may indicate presence of barbiturates, alcohol, solvents, kerosene, cationic detergents, arsenic, mercury, lead, opium paraldehyde, cyanides, carbon monoxide, phenol, salicylates, chloropromazine digitalis, mushrooms.</p>
<p><strong>Muscular Twitching and Convulsions</strong> - may result from insecticides, atropine cyanides, nicotine salicylates, amphetamine, lead, mercury, phenothiazines arsenic, kerosene, barbiturates, digitalis.</p>
<p><strong>Parethesias</strong> - from lead, thallium, DDT.</p>
<p><strong>Ataxia</strong> - as a result of lead, organophosphate, antiinstances, thallium, barbiturate,</p>
<p><strong>Headache</strong> - may point to nitroglycerin, nitrates, hydralazine, trinitrotohiene, indomethacin</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>(indocin) carbon monoxide, organic phosphoate insecticides, atropine, lead, carbon tetrachloride.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-eyes-ears-and-mouth">The Eyes, Ears and Mouth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-eyes-ears-and-mouth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The eyes may present with:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Blurred Vision</strong> - indicating atropine, phosphates ester insecticide, cocaine, nicotine methyl alcohol, indomethacin, botulism.</li>
<li><strong>Coloured Vision</strong> - indicating digitalis.</li>
<li><strong>Double Vision</strong> - suggesting alcohol, barbiturate nicotine, phosphate ester insecticides.</li>
<li><strong>Dilated Pupil</strong> - suggesting atropine, cocaine, nicotine, solvents, depressants, antihistamines phenylephrine mushrooms, thallium oleander.</li>
<li><strong>Constricted Pupil</strong> - indicating morphine phenothiazines, phosphate ester insecticides, mushrooms.</li>
<li><strong>Papilledema</strong> - suggesting lead.</li>
<li><strong>Ptosis and Strabismus</strong> - indicating botulism, thallium.</li>
<li><strong>Lacrimation</strong> - indicating organic phosphate insecticides, nicotine, mushrooms.</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient may also present with the following symptoms affecting the ears:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Tinnitus</strong> - which indicates quinine salicylates, quinidine, indomethacin.</li>
<li><strong>Deafness or disturbances of equilibrium</strong> - due to streptomycin quinine.</li>
</ul>
<p>The mouth may be affected in the following ways:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Loosening of Teeth</strong> - as a result of mercury, lead, phosphorus.</li>
<li><strong>Salivation</strong> - due to lead, mercury, bismuth, thallium, mushrooms, phosphate ester insecticides.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-cardio-respiratory-system">The Cardio Respiratory System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-cardio-respiratory-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient's cardio respiratory system may be affected which may exhibit as:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Respiratory Difficulty</strong> - due to phosphate ester insecticides, salicylates, botulism, cyanide, carbon monoxide atropine, alcohol, etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pulmonary-edema">Pulmonary Edema<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pulmonary-edema" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>due to metal fumes, hydrogen sulfide, morphine, methyl bromide, methyl chloride.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rapid-respiration">Rapid Respiration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rapid-respiration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>is due to cyanide, atropine, cocaine, carbon dioxide, salicylates, alcohol, amphetamine, mushrooms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="slow-respiration">Slow Respiration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#slow-respiration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>due to carbon monoxide barbiturates, morphine, botulism, magnesium, antihistamines, thallium fluorides.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="palpitation">Palpitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palpitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>due to nitrites, nitroglycerine, organic nitrates, potassium bromate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aspiration-pneumonia">Aspiration Pneumonia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aspiration-pneumonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>due to kerosene.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-gastrointestinal-system">The Gastrointestinal System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-gastrointestinal-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The gastrointestinal system may also be affected and the patient may exhibit the following characteristics:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Vomiting, diarrhoea, abdominal pain</strong> - due to almost all poisons.</li>
<li><strong>Bleeding</strong> - as a result of salicylates, warfarin, thallium, iron, fluorides, amnophylline, corrosive agents.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-genitourinary-system">The Genitourinary System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-genitourinary-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The genitourinary system can be affected in the following ways:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Anuria</strong> - from mercurials, bismuth, sulfonamides, carbon tetrachloride, turpentine, oxalic acid, formaldehyde, phosphorus, ethylenechlorolydrin, castor bean, trinitotothiene.</li>
<li><strong>Hematuria</strong> - due to heavy metals, for example, lead and mercury nitrates solamine and other plant poisons.</li>
<li><strong>Oliguria</strong> - as a result of lead poisoning.</li>
<li><strong>Proteinuria</strong> - from arsenic, mercury, phosphorus.</li>
<li><strong>Menstrual Irregularities</strong> - as a result of lead, bismuth, mercurials, estrogens.</li>
<li><strong>Colour of Urine</strong> - manifests as red urine (especially in warfarin and castor bean poisoning) and orange urine in hepatotoxines.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
