</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-introduction-to-the-operating-theatre">SECTION 1: INTRODUCTION TO THE OPERATING THEATRE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-introduction-to-the-operating-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this section you will briefly look at the development of operating theatre nursing, the legal aspects of operating theatre nursing and the physical layout of the theatre.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="history-of-theatre-nursing">History of Theatre Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-of-theatre-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Theatre nursing has developed alongside the history of surgery. Surgery is an old form of treatment that can be traced back through the history of man. In the past, there were no theatres, no trained personnel, no anaesthesia and no equipment. Operations were performed at home. Problems during this time included infection, bleeding and pain.</p>
<p>However, with time, efforts were made to solve these problems. For example, in 17 BC, alcohol and opium were used to relieve pain by Napoleon who performed an amputation while the patient slept for 24 hours. By 1772, Joseph Priestly discovered the use of nitrous oxide as anaesthesia, and in 1842, Dr Crawford discovered the use of ether. In 1847 James Young began to use chloroform. In the 18th century a great breakthrough was made with the use of trilene thiopentone, clytopopaine and curare, which are muscle relaxants. By the end of 19th century, pain relief was an integral part of surgery.</p>
<p>In order to control haemorrhaging, the ancient Greeks and Romans as far back as the 16th century BC, used strings as ligatures. Later on, during the Middle Ages, they came up with the use of hot iron. This idea has been developed into the use of cautery to control bleeding. By the beginning of the 20th century, many types of ligatures were available, prepared from metal, nylon and cotton.</p>
<p>The control of infection dates back to the efforts of Louis Pasteur, who proved that bacteria caused infections. In 1865, Joseph Lister used carbonic acid to reduce the growth of bacteria in wounds. In 1886 Von Bergemen introduced sterilisation of dressings.</p>
<p>You have at one time or another, used gloves while providing care. They were introduced in surgery in 1890. You are now probably thinking back and asking where theatre nursing started? This question is answered when you look back at the history of nursing. You will recall that in unit one on general nursing the history of nursing was discussed. The history of nursing is very much related to the history of theatre nursing.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 373 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Operating theatre nursing is a special branch of nursing. The theatre nurse has evolved together with the development of the theatre. They are a member of a bigger team, all of whom work together to provide a safe passage through the operating theatre for every patient. However small or insignificant the task to be performed, the theatre nurse is responsible for the success of the procedure. They must, therefore, be highly skilled and trained, in order to be able to ensure a successful outcome for the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-do-you-think-are-the-aims-of-a-theatre-nurse">What do you think are the aims of a theatre nurse?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-do-you-think-are-the-aims-of-a-theatre-nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some of the aims of the theatre nurse are:</p>
<ul>
<li>To prepare conscientiously by study to adapt to the changing world of medicine</li>
<li>To allay the fears of the patient</li>
<li>To integrate the patient care during their period in theatre</li>
<li>To become highly skilled in theatre techniques</li>
<li>To be able to impart knowledge to others</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="legal-aspects-in-theatre-nursing">Legal Aspects in Theatre Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#legal-aspects-in-theatre-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will start by looking at the term 'legal'. The dictionary defines the word legal as 'required' or 'permitted by law'. Therefore, when we talk of legal aspects in theatre nursing, we are referring to what the law requires us to do in the theatre before, during and after the operation. In your clinical practice as a nurse, you may have participated in nursing a patient who was to undergo an operation. Can you remember what preoperative care was required before the patient could go for the operation?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preoperative-care">Preoperative Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preoperative-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The preoperative care requirements are:</p>
<ol>
<li>You should make sure that the surgeon explains clearly to the patient what will happen to them.</li>
<li>The surgeon should obtain an informed consent from the patient or parent/guardian/next of kin for those under age or not in a position to sign (e.g. unconscious person).</li>
<li>The nurse ensures that the patient has signed an informed consent, after the surgeon has explained the advantages and outcomes of the operation.</li>
<li>Make sure that the patient observes a 'Nil by oral' rule.</li>
</ol>
<p>The fasting should usually start six hours before the operation.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Blood works: All should be within the acceptable ranges e.g. full Haemogram including HB, urea, electrolytes and creatinine.</li>
<li>The patient should be counselled and reassured especially those receiving operations such as amputation, or mastectomy.</li>
<li>The site to be operated on should be shaved</li>
</ol>
<p>of hair and cleaned with warm soapy water, to reduce the bacteria on the patient's skin. The area shaved should be larger than the incision site.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Catheterisation and IV branula insertion may be necessary depending on the surgery.</li>
<li>Observations of vital signs, urine testing for sugars, proteins and acetone should be done.</li>
<li>The receiving area nurse should confirm that the above preoperative measures have been taken by the ward nurse in order to allow the patient in theatre.</li>
</ol>
<p>Some of the preparations form part of the legal requirements before surgery.</p>
<p>In unit one of this module you covered nursing ethics where the importance of confidentiality in nursing practice was stressed. This is another legal requirement. In the definition of legal, the term 'permitted by law' implies that you can only carry out patient care within what the law permits you to do. Therefore, the law gives the patient seeking medical, surgical and nursing care, rights under which they are to be managed.</p>
<p>The dictionary defines rights as any claim that is morally just or legally granted as allowable or due to a person. This brings you to the term 'legal rights of an individual during theatre nursing'.</p>
<p>When it is said that a person has the legal right to informed consent, what is meant is that they must be given information regarding the type of operation to be performed, why it is necessary, and its effects both bad and good, before being requested to sign the consent form for the operation.</p>
<p>However, you must also be aware of the fact that not all patients are given all the information regarding the type of operation they are to undergo. Before you give such information, you</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>need to take factors such as age and level of education into consideration.</p>
<p>No matter how impossible it is to communicate this information to a patient, it would be against the law and their individual rights to ask them to sign the consent form for an operation when they have not fully understood the implications.</p>
<p>It is on this basis that those below the legal age of adulthood (18 years in Kenya) are not legally bound to sign the consent form. It is signed by the parents/guardians on their behalf. In the same way, consent for the mentally ill is sought from their parents/guardians/relatives. It is also important to note that consent for an operation should be obtained from the patient before they are pre-medicated, as pre-medication drugs have the potential of affecting their reasoning capacity, hence making consent signed not legally binding.</p>
<p>Having looked at confidentiality and informed consent, it is important to mention that the custody and security of the patient before, during and after operation is vested in the theatre team. It has already been implied earlier that by signing the consent form, the patient takes some responsibility for the whole loss of life or part of their body. However, this does not take away the responsibility of the theatre team to ensure the security of the patient's life during the operation.</p>
<p>The legal aspect in theatre nursing involves the care of the patient from the time the patient is accepted in theatre, until they are handed over back to the ward.</p>
<p>For these reasons, the following procedure should be adhered to:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Any patient going to theatre must be properly prepared preoperatively.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient must sign an informed consent, obtained by the surgeon.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient must be protected from any harm, falls or eventuality, during the stay in theatre.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Confidentiality must be observed regarding the patient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Measures must be taken to ensure that the patient taken to theatre is the right one for the intended operation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The items to be used for the operation must be counted and recorded before and after operation to prevent loss of swabs, tubes, blades, forceps, abdominal pacts and any instrument used.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Theatre nurses must know where the exits are, for use in case of an emergency.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sockets in theatre should be covered during scrubbing to prevent risk of conducting currents. They should also be one meter or more above the floor level.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All electrical machines must be checked to ascertain optimum function before use on the patient.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="layout-of-an-operating-theatre">Layout of an Operating Theatre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#layout-of-an-operating-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The theatre unit is a block of buildings with a series of rooms leading off a corridor with closed doors, which separate it from the main hospital.</p>
<p>The doors reduce unnecessary movement to and from theatre. A theatre should be built in a central place possibly near an intensive care unit, the surgical wards and other special wards, for example, renal unit and burns unit.</p>
<p>All these units should be in relation to each other, but construction should be separate and independent from all traffic and air movement within the hospital.</p>
<p>A theatre unit is self contained with changing rooms, shower rooms, toilets, anaesthetic room, operating room, cleaning room, at least four beds, sluice room, linen room and sterilising room.</p>
<p>Inside the theatre, the walls, floor and roof are built with labour saving materials for hygiene purposes. It has artificial ventilators, efficient artificial lights and emergency systems for use during power failure. The theatre furnishings and fittings are made of stainless materials for quick and thorough cleaning.</p>
<p>All the trolleys are fitted with non-electricity conducting rubbers to minimise the risk of electric conduction. The doors and corridors are wide and high for easy movement. The ceilings are high enough for proper theatre ventilation.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 376 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-2-safety-and-infection-prevention-in-theatre">SECTION 2: SAFETY AND INFECTION PREVENTION IN THEATRE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-safety-and-infection-prevention-in-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Safety and infection prevention are of utmost importance in the operating theatre. To ensure this, in this section you will consider the preparation of the operating theatre, theatre nurse, patient and equipment. You will also cover the equipment used in theatre and types of anaesthesia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the principles of infection prevention in the operating room</li>
<li>Describe the equipment used in the operating room</li>
<li>State the different types of anaesthesia</li>
<li>Explain the use and mode of action of local and general anaesthesia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-infection-prevention-in-the-operation-theatre">Principles of Infection Prevention in the Operation Theatre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-infection-prevention-in-the-operation-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Before you read on, try to reflect back on the rationale for safety and infection prevention in the wards.</p>
<p>To ensure safety and prevent infection in the theatre, you must consider the following points:</p>
<ul>
<li>Preparation of the operation room</li>
<li>Preparation of a theatre nurse</li>
<li>Preparation of the equipment</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at each of these in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-the-operating-room">Preparation of the Operating Room<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-the-operating-room" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The theatre and equipment must be cleaned thoroughly every morning to minimise the number of micro-organisms. Ensure high dusting of walls and clean trolleys, drip stand, operating tables and all equipment therein. You should also ensure that the floor is scrubbed with soapy water and then mopped with a disinfectant recommended by the hospital. After cleaning and drying the theatre floor, all the equipment must be returned to its proper place.</p>
<p>Prepare the operating table by drying it after cleaning and placing it in the right position directly below the overhead operating lights. It should then be draped with a clean sheet ready to receive the patient. You should then set the anaesthetic tray ready and check the anaesthetic machine to ensure it is in working order for use to cauterise any bleeding vessel during operation.</p>
<p>The operating lights should be checked to ensure they are in good working order. The required operating set of equipment should be ordered from the theatre sterilising room/unit.</p>
<p>After the operation has been completed you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Clean all fitments and equipment thoroughly</li>
<li>Do high and low level dusting using the disinfectant</li>
<li>Clean the floor and drains with the disinfectant</li>
<li>Wipe the operating lights with a clean damp towel</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-the-nurse">Preparation of the Nurse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-the-nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>After entering the theatre unit, you should go straight to the changing rooms. Take a shower and change into your theatre suit and boots. Personal clothes should be locked in a locker within the changing room. Your head should be covered with a clean, sterile theatre cap. If you have any respiratory infection you are advised not to enter the operating room. A very high standard of personal hygiene should be maintained. You should avoid movement in and out of the theatre and any time that happens you should change into another clean theatre suit before re-entering the operating room.</p>
<p>It is advisable for you to visit the toilet to empty your bowels and bladder before taking a shower and putting on the sterile theatre suit to minimise the need of using this facility later during the theatre activities. However, this is just a precautionary measure and you should change your theatre suit any time the toilet facilities are used if you are to go back to the operating room. You are now going to look at the procedure of scrubbing, gowning and gloving for the operation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scrubbing">Scrubbing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scrubbing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is done to remove micro-organisms from the forearm and arms by mechanical washing and chemical disinfections before taking part in surgical procedure. This helps prevent the possibility of the patient being contaminated by bacteria from the hands and arms.</p>
<p>Preparation for this procedure involves the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>The theatre suit should have the top/shirt tidily tucked in. Roll the sleeves up to at least three inches above the elbow.</li>
<li>A cap should be worn to cover all the hair, tie the tape at the back.</li>
<li>A mask should be worn with the short side above the nose and the long side under the chin.</li>
<li>Remove all jewellery, wide wedding rings, dress rings, watches, earrings and necklaces.</li>
<li>Finger nails must be short and clean without nail varnish.</li>
<li>No cut wounds or septic wound on fingers.</li>
<li>No upper respiratory tract infection.</li>
<li>No gastroenteritis.</li>
<li>Wear a mackintosh apron to protect your scrub suit.</li>
<li>Regulate temperature and flow of water to suit you.</li>
<li>Scrubbing time varies according to the type of soap or chemical used. For example, if using gamophen soap, which contains hexachlorophene disinfectants, you should scrub for five minutes; if using hibiscrub, two minutes; ordinary soap, ten to fifteen minutes.</li>
</ul>
<p>The following procedure should be followed for a complete scrub:</p>
<ol>
<li>Use the wall clock to time yourself.</li>
<li>Wet the hands and arms to the elbow.</li>
<li>Pick the soap and make a lot of lather on the hands and arms (the soap remains in hands until the point of drop off later).</li>
<li>Wash hands and arms for one minute. This is called a social wash.</li>
<li>Keeping the fingertips uppermost all the time, rinse hands to the elbow.</li>
<li>Using the elbow, press the hutch of the dispenser and pick one sterile brush. Lather the brush and keep tablet of soap at back of the brush between your palm and brush in your right hand.</li>
<li>Starting with the left hand put your fingers together and scrub the fingernails. Move to the fingers, and then wipe off the hand and palm. Use a circular movement inside the palm.</li>
</ol>
<p>Spend extra time at the folds of the wrist. Do this for <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1 \frac{1}{2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> minutes, rinsing often and starting again.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Rinse the hands from fingertips to wrists after the <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1 \frac{1}{2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> minutes. Rinse the brush and soap as well.</li>
<li>Change over to the right hand and repeat the procedures (7) - (8). Spend another <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1 \frac{1}{2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> minutes. Drop the bush into the correct receptacle provided. Keep the soap still in hands.</li>
<li>Lather hands and wash up to the wrist for another minute. Rinse the soap and drop it back into the soap dish.</li>
<li>Take all necessary precautions to avoid touching the tap handles during this exercise as this contaminates the hands.</li>
<li>Rinse the hands and arms thoroughly in one direction only starting from fingertips working down systematically to elbows.</li>
<li>Close the taps using elbows. Keep hands together upright, fingers higher than elbows. A total of five to ten minutes have been observed during the procedure.</li>
<li>The circulating nurse will remove the mackintosh apron.</li>
</ol>
<p>There are set procedures for drying, gowning and gloving.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drying">Drying<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drying" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pick up the towel and step back. Start with the left hand and blot dry the fingers, the webs of the hand and the palm well. and then move to the back of the hand, and the forearm, using a circular movement to the elbows. Change the towel to the left hand with the wet part against the left palm. Using the dry part of the towel, repeat the same procedure on the other arm. When you get to the elbow, discard the used towel in the dispenser provided.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gowning">Gowning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gowning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when gowning:</p>
<ol>
<li>Pick a gown and step back.</li>
<li>Hold the neck-band and let the bottom hem drop.</li>
</ol>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Open the gown and slide both hands in through the arm holes.</li>
<li>Do not touch the outside of the gown with your bare hands.</li>
<li>The Runner Nurse will first tie the neck and shoulder bands then wristbands without touching the gown.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gloving">Gloving<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gloving" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure should be adhered to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Arrange gloves on the trolley with glove finger portion away from you.</li>
<li>Pick the glove with left hand holding at the folded part and slip in your right hand. Fold the tip of the sleeve on right hand and pass the glove over.</li>
<li>Using the gloved hand slip your fingers beneath the folded area of the remaining glove and slip in the left hand into the glove.</li>
<li>Unroll the cuff of the glove covering the cuff of the sleeve.</li>
<li>Do the same for the opposite hand using the same technique.</li>
<li>Ensure you do not contaminate any area that will come in contact with the sterile field.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patient-s-skin-preparation">Patient's Skin Preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-s-skin-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Skin preparation depends on the area being operated.</p>
<p>Preparation of the skin includes vigorous sponging of the skin with a sponge soaked in strong disinfectant held in a sponge holding forceps.</p>
<p>Disinfectants used include centrimide and hibitine in spirit. After sponging, the area is swabbed once with iodine in spirit or hibitine 5% in 70% alcohol.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="draping-of-patient">Draping of Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#draping-of-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The purpose of draping is to maintain an adequate sterile field for the surgical procedure.</p>
<p>The scrub nurse gives the surgeon the sterile towel to cover the area above the operation site and below and the sides.</p>
<p>After draping, the scrub nurse brings the operation trolley and instrument trolley next to the table.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="positioning-of-patient">Positioning of Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positioning-of-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Positioning is done by the other team members who have not scrubbed up and worn sterile gowns and gloves. Patients are positioned before the skin preparation and draping described previously.</p>
<p>This involves placing the patient on the operating table to a desirable level for surgery and ensures that any harm to the patient, such as pressure on the nerves, is prevented. After positioning, the theatre gown is removed and skin prepared.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="trendelenburg">Trendelenburg<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trendelenburg" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trendelenburg, which is most commonly used in pelvic operations, where the patient is placed supine and the head lowered and the table is broken at the knee joint to lower the lower section slightly to flex the patient's knees.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-dd6757c2.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kidney-position">Kidney position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kidney-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Kidney position, where the bridge of the table is raised to elevate the loins between the lower limbs and the iliac crest.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-6b6a4f52.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lithotomy">Lithotomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lithotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lithotomy, which is used in perineum operation. The patient lies supine and the lower limbs are raised on stirrups from the pelvis. Both legs must be raised simultaneously to avoid injury. The knees are flexed.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-5421b6af.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laminectomy">Laminectomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laminectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Laminectomy position, where the patient is put in the prone position with the head beyond the end of the table with the forehead resting and supported on a horseshoe fixed six inches below the level of the table.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-92b0a070.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supine-laparatomy-position">Supine (laparatomy position)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supine-laparatomy-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Supine (laparatomy position), where the patient lies on the back with arms on the sides on arm boards.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-f812afaa.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="equipment-used-in-theatre">Equipment Used in Theatre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#equipment-used-in-theatre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are now going to look at the equipment that is normally used during an operation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ligatures-and-sutures">Ligatures and Sutures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ligatures-and-sutures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A suture is a stitch or series of stitches used in surgery to bring together living tissues until the normal healing process takes place. A ligature is a suture used for tying blood vessels to arrest bleeding.</p>
<p>There are two types of sutures. They can be absorbable, which means they dissolve in the tissue after some time, for example, catgut. They can also be non-absorbable, which means that the body tissue cannot digest the material used, for example, silkworm gut, nylon, cotton, linen, silk and metal.</p>
<p>The latter must be removed when the wound is healed. Metal clips are also available and are used in neuro-surgery to compress nerve endings, and also on skin incision to give a good grip. Traumatic sutures are used together with a needle for suturing the skin. Ligatures are lengths of suture material used without a needle to tie a blood vessel in order to control or arrest bleeding. Most ligatures are non-absorbable, for example, those made of linen, cotton, silk, polyester, wire and clips. Absorbable include chromic catgut. Metal clips can be used as ligatures.</p>
<p>Cutting needles, which have a sharp edge, cut a crack as they pass, and are used on strong tissues, for example, skin, tendon, muscles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-needles">Surgical Needles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-needles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are made from plated carbon steel or stainless steel. The different parts of a needle are the eye, shaft, and point. The needle is either straight or curved. There are different classes of needles. These include:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="round-bodied-needles">Round bodied needles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#round-bodied-needles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Cutting needles, which have a sharp edge, cut a crack as they pass, and are used on strong tissues, for example, skin, tendon, muscles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="atraumatic-needles">Atraumatic needles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#atraumatic-needles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Round bodied needles, which are round and smooth, cause less damage and make a puncture. They are used in delicate tissues and organs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cutting-needles">Cutting needles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cutting-needles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Atraumatic needles, which are either cutting or round bodied whose traumatising chance is</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>minimal. These needles have no eye. Suture and needles are made joined-together.</p>
<p>This is a set of instruments that are used for a general operation. (see Houghton et al [1967] p.105 - 109) for more detailed information including photographs.</p>

<p>Equipment</p>
<p>It is important to note that dirty and unsterile equipment can become a source of infection. To reduce this, all dirty equipment must be soaked in a standard disinfectant preferably Jik, for ten minutes. This makes it safe for handling and cleaning. It should then be cleaned in soap water, rinsed, dried and then taken for autoclaving. The same should be done to linen, for example, towels, abdominal draping sheets, and gowns, which become contaminated during the operation.</p>

Bishops Computers</p>
